Dear Ms. Gonzalez: 
This report summarizes our earthwork observation and testing services performed 
during the site grading operations for the Cottages at Mauna Olu Site Improvements from 
August 5, 2021 through February 27, 2024. 
Makai Vistas at Makaha LLC 
Page 2 
W.O. 7510-60 (Grading Permit Nos. GP2020-03-01808, GP2021-03-0115, and GP2023-03-0082) 
May 31, 2024 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California  
EARTHWORK OPERATIONS 
The project site is generally located at the Phases 1A & 1B areas within the 
Mauna`olu Estates development in Makaha in the District of Waianae on the Island of 
Oahu, Hawaii. The project location and general vicinity are shown on the Project Location 
Map, Plate 1.  Based on the information provided, we understand that site grading work 
consisting of both cuts and fills will be performed to create building pads for the 
construction of about 118 new homes.  The project site is shown on the Site Plan, Plate 
2. 
J.J.S. Construction Inc. performed the site grading operations for the project. The 
site grading work consisted of subgrade preparation, placement and compaction of fills 
and backfills, pavement construction, and utility trench excavation and backfill. 
Following the clearing and grubbing operations, the over-excavated subgrades and 
areas designated to receive fills were scarified to a depth of about 12 inches, 
moisture-conditioned to above the optimum moisture content, and recompacted to a 
minimum of 90 percent relative compaction, as appropriate.  Prior to the foundation and 
slab-on-grade work at the building pads, the subgrade soils were generally 
moisture-conditioned to above the optimum moisture content and compacted to at least 90 
percent relative compaction. 
Fill and backfill materials required for the project were generally placed in near-level 
lifts, brought to above the optimum moisture, and compacted to a minimum of 90 percent 
relative compaction.  The compaction requirement was increased to a minimum of 
95 percent relative compaction for areas subjected to vehicular traffic.  Relative 
compaction refers to the in-place dry density of soil expressed as a percentage of the 
maximum dry density of the same soil established in accordance with ASTM D1557. 
Optimum moisture is the water content (percentage by weight) corresponding to the 
maximum dry density. 
New imported fills required for the project generally consisted of 3-inch minus 
non-expansive select granular material imported from Grace Pacific Quarry.  During 
placement of the non-expansive select granular fill material, the fill materials were 
generally placed in 8-inch near-level loose lifts, brought to above the optimum moisture 
content, and compacted to a minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry density 
determined in accordance with ASTM D1557 (Modified Proctor). The compaction 
requirement for the fill materials below the pavements was increased to a minimum of 95 
percent of the maximum dry density determined in accordance with ASTM D1557 
(Modified Proctor). 
During the site grading operations, samples of the on-site and imported materials 
utilized as fill materials were obtained and transported to our office for testing. The 
maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents were established in our laboratory 
in general accordance with ASTM D1557 (Modified Proctor), and the test results are 
summarized on Plate 3 of this report. 
Makai Vistas at Makaha LLC 
Page 3 
W.O. 7510-60 (Grading Permit Nos. GP2020-03-01808, GP2021-03-0115, and GP2023-03-0082) 
May 31, 2024 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California  
Field density tests were performed during the fill operations on an as-need basis to 
confirm our field observations as variations in construction procedures and soil conditions 
were noted. A total of 1,704 field density tests, including retesting of failed areas, were 
performed using the nuclear probe method in accordance with ASTM D6938. Results of 
the compaction tests performed are summarized on Plates 4.1 through 4.72 of this report. 
These tests were performed on the prepared ground surfaces and on constructed fills at 
the site. Test locations and elevations were estimated by pacing and interpolating from 
on-site survey stakes. These locations and elevations should be considered accurate only 
to the degree implied by the methods used. Areas assessed as unsatisfactory were 
reworked until the specified minimum compaction was obtained by retesting and/or 
probing with a steel rod. 
Based on the observations of our field representatives and the results of the 
referenced tests, it is our opinion that the earthwork operations during the site grading for 
the above project observed and tested by Geolabs in the period covered by this report 
were performed in general accordance with the intent of the project plans and 
specifications, and our geotechnical engineering recommendations presented in the 
referenced reports, dated August 9, 2017 and August 27, 2018, addendum dated 
June 12, 2020, and subsequent recommendations. 
LIMITATIONS 
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities 
occurring simultaneously on a construction site. Therefore, some of the earthworks may 
have been performed without our observation. However, the level of earthwork 
observation and testing services provided appears to be reasonable in reducing some 
of the geotechnical risks to the project. It should be recognized that there are variations 
in the accuracy and statistical repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor 
earthwork construction and materials.  
Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of 
geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is expressed or implied. The provision of 
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance, nor does it guarantee 
construction of any type. The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the 
work, for adhering to the plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of 
when they are found.
